arsulegai (Wed, 20 Feb 2019 16:45:20 GMT):
Yes, there's a reason for Dockerfiles. I can remove explicit passing of environment variables from compose files though for docker client versions > 17

arsulegai (Wed, 20 Feb 2019 16:46:44 GMT):
Reason for Dockerfile is explained here https://askubuntu.com/questions/53146/how-do-i-get-add-apt-repository-to-work-through-a-proxy/252082#252082 It's to deal with gnupg bug, that it fails to pick up http_proxy environment variable. There's a loophole in code that allows us to however set it explicitly through "--keyserver-options"

arsulegai (Thu, 28 Mar 2019 08:01:28 GMT):
@amundson @jsmitchell @rbuysse @rberg2 Are we fine with the approach mentioned by @danintel in the PR https://github.com/hyperledger/sawtooth-core/pull/1974

amundson (Thu, 28 Mar 2019 13:34:26 GMT):
@arsulegai not really. I'd rather see this proxy stuff purged completely from the files. I've been brainstorming a bit on how we might fix this problem in a more elegant way. One idea I have is to put a marker in each Dockerfile, then write a "add proxy workaround to Dockerfiles" script that can replace the marker with the proxy boilerplate. For normal use, the proxy code would not exist in the Dockerfiles

amundson (Thu, 28 Mar 2019 13:36:37 GMT):
we could generate "Dockerfile-proxy" files and associated docker compose proxy files

arsulegai (Fri, 29 Mar 2019 04:09:49 GMT):
@danintel @amolk ^

danintel (Fri, 29 Mar 2019 04:30:35 GMT):
Today I have removed the proxy boilerplate...example below... So the proxy stuff is implicit in environment variables or in a few places CLI parameters. See my latest PR https://github.com/hyperledger/sawtooth-seth/pull/95/ Example ``` if [ ! -z $HTTP_PROXY ] && [ -z $http_proxy ]; then \ http_proxy=$HTTP_PROXY; \ fi; \ if [ ! -z $HTTPS_PROXY ] && [ -z $https_proxy ]; then \ https_proxy=$HTTPS_PROXY; \ fi ```
